  • рдЕрд▓реНрдкреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рд╕реНрд╡рдпреЛрдирд┐рд╖реНрд╡реН рдПрдХрд╡рдВрд╢реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдХрддрд┐рдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрд╣рд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЛ рд╜рдзрд┐рдХрдГ рд╕ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдардГ ред рдХрд┐рдпрд╛рдиреН рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкрдХрд╛рд▓рдГ ред рди рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдЕрдмреНрджрдГ ред рддреНрд░реНрдпрдмреНрджрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд▓реНрдкреЗрдиреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реН рддрддреЛ рдиреНрдпреВрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдПрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рди рд╡рд░реНрд╖рджреНрд╡рдпрдореН ред рдирд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдПрдХреЛ рд╜рдмреНрджрдГ, рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкреЗрдиреЗрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрд╢реЗрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреБрдкрдкрддреНрддреЗрдГ ред рдкрд░рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдирдкрд░рд┐рдорд╛рдгреЛ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрдмреНрджрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпреЛ рд╜рд░реНрдерд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рдиреНрдпреВрдирд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рдмреНрджрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреН рдЕрд▓реНрдкреЗрдиреЗрддрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рджреН рдЕрд╡рд░рд╢реН рдЪ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реН рдЪреИрд╡ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрд▓реНрдкреЗрдиреИрд╡ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рд╕рдЦреНрдпрдореН, рдмрд╣реБрдирд╛ рддреБ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдарддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡ ред рдПрддрдЪреН рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдПрддреЗрди рд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рддрд╕рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдХрдореН рдЖрд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдореН ред

  • рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рд╡реНрдпрдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ ред рдирд╛рдиреЗрди рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░рддреНрд╡рдВ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ, рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рд╕рдЦрд┐рддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡ ред рдпрдерд╛рд╢реНрд░реБрддрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреЗрди рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕реНрдпрддреН, “рдЗрдпрддрд╛ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рд╕рдЦрд╛ рдкрд░рддрд╕реН рддреБ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдардГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдпрдВ рдЪ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рдПрдХрддреНрд░ рдкреБрд░реЗ рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рджрд╢рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдгрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ ред рдХрд▓рд╛рд╢реН рдЪрддреБрдГрд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╕реН рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрднрд┐рд░реН рд╡рд░реНрд╖реИрдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рдпреЛрдирд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдЪ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд╕рддрд╛рдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡ ред рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛ рд╡рдпрд╕рд╛ рддреБрд▓реНрдпреЛ рд╡рдпрд╕реНрдпрдГ, рдХрд┐рдВ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡ ред рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╡рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡реЗ рдЪреИрддрд▓реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН22 ред

  • рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рдПрддрддреН ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддреВрддреНрддрд░рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рд░реБрдзреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╣рд┐ рдЬрд╛рддреЗрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрдореН, рди рд╡рдпрд╕рдГ ред рдпрджрд┐ рдЪрд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдпрддрд╛ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рдЬреНрдпреИрд╖реНрдареНрдпрдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЖрд╢рдЩреНрдХреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рди рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддреНрдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЪ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рд░ рдЖрджреНрдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдВ рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее реи.резрейрек рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

It has been said above (under 120) that тАШthe life-breaths of the younger men rush outwards at the approach of the elder now the present verse proceeds to determine by bow many years one may be regarded as an тАШelderтАЩ; among ordinary men people come to be regarded as тАШelderlyтАЩ when they become grey-headed.

Among citizens, equality and friendship are regarded as subsisting among people who differ in their age by ten years, so that among these, one conies to be regarded as тАШelderтАЩ when he happens to be more than ten years older; and those less than that should be treated as тАШfriends and equalsтАЩ; and hence accosted as тАШOh, Sir,тАЩ as declared by Gautama (6.14)тАФтАЬEquals in age should be accosted as тАШOh, SirтАЩ; when the difference in age is more than ten years, the person should be regarded as тАШelder.тАЩ

In the expression тАШda┼Ы─Бbd─Бkhya,тАЩ тАШ─Бkhy─БтАЩ stands for тАШ─Бkhy─Бnam,тАЩ тАШdescriptionтАЩ; and the compound, a three-termed Bahuvr─лhi, means тАШthat whose description is ten yearsтАЩ; the years being construed as qualifying тАШfriendshipтАЩ on the basis of тАШdescription,тАЩ and no significance being attached to the difference between cause and effect (the тАШyearsтАЩ being the cause of the тАШfriendshipтАЩ), all that the compound means is thatтАФтАШone who is senior by about ten years is an equal friend.тАЩ

тАШPauras,тАЩ тАШcitizens,тАЩ are тАШpersons living in cities.тАЩ The mention of тАШcitiesтАЩ is only by way of illustration; the same rule holds good among inhabitants of villages also. Among people living in the same village, all those come to be regarded as тАШfriendsтАЩ among whom there happens to be some ground for close intimacy.

Those persons who practise some sort of artтАФcrafts, music and the rest,тАФamong these one who is older by less than five years is an тАШequalтАЩ; beyond that, he is тАШelder.тАЩ

тАШTryabdamтАЩ means тАШthat which is preceded by three yearsтАЩ; and of this kind is the тАШequalityтАЩ among learned men.

тАШAmong blood-relations, it ranges within a very short period of timeтАЩ;тАФi.e., among persons belonging to the same family, he who is senior by only a few days is also тАШelder.тАЩ

тАЬWhat period of time is to be regarded as very short?тАЭ

It cannot he three years; for having spoken of three тАШyears,тАЩ the text mentions тАШshort,тАЩ which means that it must be less than that. It cannot mean two years, because of the singular number. Nor lastly, can it mean one year, as in that case there would be no point in the qualification тАШvery short.тАЩ Because тАШyearтАЩ is the name given to a well-defined period of time; so that a period of time which is less than that even by a single day ceases to be a тАШyear.тАЩ For these reasons тАШshortтАЩ must refer to time in general (unspecified), the only peculiarity being tbat it, should be less than a year.

The particle тАШcaтАЩ should be taken as standing for тАШ?va,тАЩ тАШonlyтАЩ; the meaning being тАШfriendship ranges only within a very short period of time, beyond that the man becomes elder.тАЩ All this should be taken as holding good only among people of the same caste, possessed of similar qualifications; so that the definition of тАШelderтАЩ as something relative in sense is that obtaining among ordinary people.

Other persons explain the verso as follows:тАФThis verse does not define what is tho characteristic of being тАШelderтАЩ; it only serves to define тАШFriendship.тАЩ It could be taken as defining тАШelderlinessтАЩ only if we abandoned its direct meaning; as only then could it be taken to mean that тАШduring such time one is a friend, and after that he becomes an elder.тАЩ As a matter of fact, what the verse means is as follows:тАФ(a) People who live in the same city for ten years become тАШfriendsтАЩ; (b) among people knowing the artsтАФsixty-four in numberтАФcompanionship during five years establishes тАШfriendshipтАЩ; (c) among blood-relations, friendship is established by living together even for a very short time. Thus then, one does not become a тАШfriendтАЩ simply because he happens to be of equal age, in fact the тАШfriendтАЩ is as described; but the said conditions of тАШfriendshipтАЩ all require tbat the parties concerned be of equal age.

All this may be true; but this explanation is inconsistent with the next verse; in the latter, тАШcasteтАЩ is mentioned as the pre-eminent factor, and not the age; and the reason is that if the mere fact of being so many years older in age were to make one тАШelder,тАЩ then we could not get rid of the contingency of persons of different (and inferior) castes being regarded as тАШelders.тАЩ

Older commentators have all adopted the first explanation (put forward by us).тАФ(134)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАЬThose who are тАШfriendsтАЩ and equals may address each other with the words тАШbhoс╕етАЩ, тАШbhavat,тАЩ or тАШvayasyaтАЩ, тАШfriendтАЩ. The explanation of the verse, which is substantially the same in all the commentaries, is based on GautamaтАЩs passage (6.14-17); while HaradattaтАЩs interpretation of ─Аpastamba (1.4.13) somewhat differs.тАЭтАФ(Buhler).

тАЬA small difference in age constitutes among relatives a difference in position; but in other cases only a considerable difference as specified.тАФThis тАШequalityтАЩ refers to the form of salutation among equals.тАЭтАФ(BurnellтАФHopkins).

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 466), where the following explanation is given:тАФAmong persons living in the same city, and not possessed of any exceptional learning or wealth or other qualifications, if the difference in the age of two persons extends to within ten years, they are to treat each other as тАШfriends,тАЩ and there is to be no salutation; the тАШcityтАЩ here includes the village also;тАФamong persons versed in music and other arts, equality extends to within five years of difference in age;тАФand among those learned in the Veda to within one (as read here) year;тАФand among Sapiс╣Зс╕Нas, to within a very short period of time. In every case there is тАШsuperorityтАЩ if the difference exceeds the periods mentioned.

It is quoted also in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 299), where also we have the following explanation Among inhabitants of the same village one is to be treated as тАШfriendтАЩ if he is older by less than ten years; beyond that he is to be treated as тАШsuperiorтАЩ.тАФAmong men expert in the arts and in learning, there is equality if there is a difference of five years;тАФamong persons learned in the Veda, or students of the Veda, there is equality if there is a difference of three years, after which the older man becomes тАШsuperiorтАЩ;тАФamong blood relations, brothers and the rest, the older person is to be treated as an equal only when the difference in age is very small.

Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava raises the question of saluting such с╣Ъtvik and others as are younger in age. In view of the general rule that these should be saluted, the fact of any one being younger in age does not deprive him of his right to a salute. The conclusion however is that all that is meant is that they have to be тАШtreated with respectтАЩ; and this implies that one should stand up to receive and welcome them with agreeable words, as is clearly laid down by Baudh─Бyana, who says,

с╣Ыtvik┼Ыva┼Ыurapitс╣Ы?yam─Бtul─Бn─Бс╣Г tu yaviyas─Бс╣Г pratyutth─Бn─Бbhibh─Бс╣гaс╣Зam.

That these are not to he saluted is clearly asserted by Gautama (6.9), which lays down that these are anabhiv─Бth─Бс╕е (?), It is interesting to note that in quoting Gautama, M─Бdhava has read abhiv─Бdanam in place of anabhiv─Бdy─Бс╕е; but knowing somehow that the meaning of Gautama was that these are not abhiv─Бdy─Бс╕е, he has explained abhiv─Бdanam as abhibh─Бс╣гaс╣Зam, speech.

The verse is quoted also in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 29) as declaring the difference in age which constitutes тАШsuperiorityтАЩ. It practically repeats the explanation given in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (see above); but at the end adds that among blood-relations, the difference of even one day establishes superiority; while between relations born on the same day there is equality as declared by ─Аpastamba.тАФтАШOne born on the same day is a friend.тАЩ

Apar─Бrka (p. 53) quotes this verse and adds the following explanation:тАФAmong citizens even one who is ten years older is a тАШfriend and it is only one who is more than ten years older is to be regarded as an тАШelderтАЩ; among musicians and other artists one older by five years or less is a тАШfriendтАЩ, older than that he becomes an тАШelderтАЩ; among Vedic scholars, it is upto three years; and among these latter, superority or inferiority is determined by special qualifications.тАФ-The particle тАШapiтАЩ means тАШevaтАЩ.

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 101), which offers the following explanation:тАФAmong citizens, one who is senior by one to ten years is to be regarded as a тАШfriendтАЩтАФan equal; one older than that is an тАШelderтАЩтАФa superior;тАФamong artists people versed in singing, dancing and so forth there is тАШfriendshipтАЩ upto a difference of five years; among Vedic scholars it extends to a difference of three years; older than that, is тАШelderтАЩтАФsuperior; among blood-relations there is тАШfriendshipтАЩ within a limit of very few years; one even a little older is to be saluted like an тАШelderтАЩ;тАФall this refers to Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra (1.24.13).тАФтАШFriendship (equality) among citizens extends up to ten years; among members of the same Vedic sect, up to five years and the elder Vedic scholar deserves salutation if he is senior by three years.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra (6.2.5).тАФтАШOne born on the same day as oneself is his friend; a citizen who is senior by ten years; an artisan, who is senior by five years; a Vedic scholar of the same Vedic sect, who is senior by three years.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

One since whose birth ten years have elapsed is тАШof ten years.тАЩ The time is the determining and the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa the determined factor; but it is not possible to determine, by means of time, either his tallness or shortness or thinness, etc.; what can be determined by it is only a certain act of his; and this act can only be that of maintaining his life-breath, which subsists in him continuously since his birth.

The same explanation applies to the epithet тАШof a hundred years.тАЩ

They should be looked upon as тАШfather and son.тАЩ

тАШOf the twoтАЩтАФas compared with each other,тАФтАЩ the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is the father.тАЩ

All that this means is that even when the Kс╣гatriya is very old and the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa very young in years, the former should rise to meet and salute the latter.тАФ(135)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 474), as showing that the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is тАШsuperiorтАЩ to all.

It quotes the same verse as contained in Bhaviс╣гyapur─Бс╣Зa.тАФ. It is quoted also in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 44b);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 101) to the effect that as between a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and a Kс╣гatriya, the former is to be saluted by the latter, even though he be very much junior in age.

  • рдЕрдереЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред “рд╡реЗрджрдГ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдиреЛ рд╜рдзрд┐рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ” (рдореНрдзреН реи.резремрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирд╡реЗрджрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реН рдЕрд╡рдмреЛрдзрдкрд░реНрдпрдиреНрддрдГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реЗрджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╡рдмреЛрдзреЗ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпреЗ рдХреБрддреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рд╡рдмреЛрдзрд╕рдВрднрд╡рдГ, рдпреЗрдиреЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ “рдпреЛ рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╡реЗрддреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдПрдХрд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирдВ рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддрддреНрд░ рдпреЗрдиреИрдХрд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдзреАрддрд╛ рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢реН рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рд╡рдзреГрддрдГ, рд╕реЛ рд╜рдирд╡рдзреГрддрд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░реИрдХ рдПрд╡ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджрд┐ рдирд╛рдо рдкрджрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрднреЗрджрдГ, рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд░реВрдкрдВ рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрднрд┐рдиреНрдирдореН26 ред рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рд╡рдмреЛрдзрдГ ред рди рдЪ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╢рд╛рдЦрдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рднрд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ27 ред рдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдпреЗрдиреИрд╡ рд╣реЗрддреБрдиреИрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдпрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рд╡рдзрд░реНрдпрддреЗ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╜рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐, рди рд╡реНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдпрджреНрдпреН рдПрдХрд╛ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рд╡рдЧрддрд╛, рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдПрд╡рд╛рд╡рдЧрддрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред

  • рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН ред рдпрд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдиреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╜рдкреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдорд╛ рднреВрджреН рднреЗрджрдГ28 ред рдХрд┐рдВ рддреБ рдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд┐рдЪреН рдЫрд╛рдЦрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдХрд╛рдирд┐рдЪрд┐рддреН рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдиреИрд╡реЛрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдмрд╛рд╣реНрд╡реГрдЪреЗ рдЖрд╢реНрд╡рд▓рд╛рдпрдирдХреЗ рджрд░реНрд╢рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕реМ рд╢реНрдпреЗрдирд╛рджрд┐рд░реН рдЖрднрд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рдХрдГ29, рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗ рдЪ рд╕реЛрдордпрд╛рдЧрд╡рд╛рдЬрдкреЗрдпрдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рд╕рд╡рд╛рджрдпрдГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдпрддреН рддрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдЦрд╛рдзреАрдирдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛрдорд╛рджрд┐ рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдзрд┐рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдирдзреАрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд░реБрддрдВ рдХрдердВ рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐30 рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпреН рддрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдЦрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреА рд╡реЗрддреНрддреБ ред рди рдЪреИрддреЗ рд╕реЛрдордпрд╛рдЧрд╛ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛, рдпреЗрдирд╛рдирдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдпрднрдпрд╛рддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЖрдзрд╛рдирдВ рддреБ рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рддрддреНрд░ рди рдкрдард┐рддрдВ рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпреН “рдЙрджреНрдзрд░рд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрдореН” (рдРрддреНрдмреН рел.реирем; рдЖрд╢реНрд╢реН реи.реи.рез) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рддреН рддрджрд░реНрдердореН рдЕрдирд╡рдмреБрдзреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдХреЛ рд╜рдпрдореН рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзрд╛рдирдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред рддрддрдГ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдкрдареНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЖрдзрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рдХрд░рдгрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рд▓реЛрдЪрдпрддрд┐ ред рдПрд╡рдореН рдЖрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдпреЗрди рд╡рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреМрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕реЗрди рд╡реЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореН рдЕрдирдпреЛрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгреЛ рд░реВрдкрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдЧрд╡реЗрд╖рдпрддреЗ ред рдПрд╡рдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрджреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдпрддреН рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдВ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдареЗрдпрдВ рддрд╕реНрдп рдпрддреН рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрдЬрд╛рддрдВ рддрддреНрд░ рдирд╛рдореНрдирд╛рддрдореН рдЖрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рдореН рдФрджреНрдЧрд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд╛ рддрддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп рддрдереИрд╡ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдзрд┐рдЧрдордГ31 ред рдпрддреН рддреБ рд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдзреАрддрдореН рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдареЗрдпрдВ рддрд╕реНрдп рди рд╡реЗрджрдирд╕рдВрднрд╡рдГ ред рдЕрдиреЗрдХрд╢рд╛рдЦрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд┐рдирд╕реН рддреБ рддрджрд░реНрдердкрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореН рдПрддрддреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдореН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реНрддреАрджреГрд╢реАрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реЗрдгрд╛рдкрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдореН ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдИрд╖рджреНрд╡реНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдВ ред
  • рдпрд╕реНрдп рддреБ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд▓рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛, рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐, рддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрддрд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдореН32 ред рдЧрд░реАрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рдпреЛрд░реН рджреНрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗ рд╜рдпрдореН рдИрдпрд╕реБрдиреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдердирдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдкрдЩреНрдЧреНрд╡рдиреНрдзрдирд┐рд░реНрдзрдирд╛рджрд┐рд░реН рдЕрдирдзрд┐рдХреГрддреЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдпреИрд╡ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ ред
  • рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзреЗ рдмрд▓рд╛рдмрд▓рдореН рдЖрд╣- рдЧрд░реАрдпреЛ рдпрджреН рдпрджреН рдЙрддреНрддрд░рдореН ред рдПрдХрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдмрд╣реБрдмрдиреНрдзреБрддрд╛, рддрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрд╡рддреЛ рдмрдиреНрдзреБрдорд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдГ ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рдпрддреН рдкрд░рдВ рддрддреН рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреН рдЧреБрд░реБрддрд░рдореН33 ред рддрдерд╛ рдмрдиреНрдзреЛрд░реН рд╡рдпрдГ рддрддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд╛рджреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрд╛рддреН рддрджреН рдЧреБрд░реБ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН ред рдЕрдд рдЙрдкрдкрдиреНрдирдореН “рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдВ рддреБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдЧрд░реАрдпрд╕реН рддрдиреНрдореВрд▓рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдзрд░реНрдорд╕реНрдп” рдЗрддрд┐ рдЧреМрддрдорд╡рдЪрдирдореН (рдЧреНрдзреН рем.реирезтАУреиреи) ред
  • рдЧрд░реАрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрдердВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпреЛ рдпрд╛рд╡рддрд╛ рдиреИрд╡ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЧреБрд░реБрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдпрджрд┐ рд╣рд┐ рджреНрд╡реЗ рдЧреБрд░реБрдгреА34 рддрддреНрд░реЛрддреНрддрд░реАрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЧрд░реАрдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН, рд╕рдореБрджрд╛рдпреЗ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрди рдЧреБрд░реБрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреЗ рдЕрдкрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдд рдИрдпрд╕реВрдиреН ред
  • рдорд╛рдирдГ рдкреВрдЬрд╛ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдВ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдореН ред “рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рдареЗ рд╜рдиреНрддрд░реНрднреВрддрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред “рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐” рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрддреНрд╡рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рее реи.резрейрем рее

рдПрдХреИрдХрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреЗ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдпрддреНрд░реЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рджреНрд╡реМ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╡реН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдп рднрд╡рддреЛ рд╜рдкрд░рд╕реНрдпреИрдХрдГ рдкрд░ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрддреНрд░ рдХрдердореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдд рдЖрд╣ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Caste has been described as a ground of superiority; so that one belonging to a higher caste should be respected by one of a lower caste. The text now proceeds to describe the relative strength of those factors that entitle persons of a caste to salutation and honour among themselves.

Age is mentioned here again only for the purpose of indicating its position as compared with others.

In the case of all that is mentioned here it is the connection of the person with them that entitles him to respect. That is, the possession of wealth and the possession of relations constitute titles of respect. It is not meant that the peculiar relationship borne by the manтАФsuch as that of being a paternal or a maternal uncleтАФconstitutes the title of respect; what is meant is that one who has many relations deserves to be respected.

тАШAgeтАЩтАФi.e., advanced age. The term is generally used in this qualified sense ; e. g., in such passages asтАФтАШEven though the son be of age, he should be advised by his father.тАЩ Verse 134 has already explained what age entitles one to respect

тАШActionтАЩтАФsuch as is laid down in ┼Ъrutis and Smс╣Ыtis; i. e., oneтАЩs assiduity in performing such actions.

тАШLearning,тАЩтАФthe knowledge of the Veda along with the subsidiary sciences and their auxiliaries.

Objection.тАФтАЬIn view of such declarations as тАШthe learned man offers sacrifices,тАЩ тАШthe learned man officiates at sacrifices,тАЩ the unlearned person can never be entitled to the performance of religious acts; under the circumstances, how can mere тАШaction,тАЩ without тАШlearning,тАЩ be a ground for respect?тАЭ

Answer.тАФThere is no force in this objection. Excellence is what is meant here. Superior or efficient learning is what constitutes a title to respect; and as for the performance of actions, this can be done also by men possessed of limited learning; for a man is entitled to perform actions in accordance with the knowledge possessed by him: specially as тАШlearningтАЩ entitles a person to the performance of actions simply because it serves to capacitate him for it, and not because it has been declared to be a necessary condition.

тАЬBut the man devoid of learning cannot know the form of the action to be performed, and being capable of acting only like lower animals, to the performance of what could he be entitled?тАЭ

Even such a person can, on having heard a few Smс╣Ыti-texts, perform austerities and repeat mantras. It is only in the performance of the Agnihotra and such other Vedic rites that one requires the knowledge of Vedic texts. But here also the title to perform the rites is dependent upon the extent of knowledge possessed by the man; e.g., one who knows the meaning of tho texts bearing upon the Agnihotra is entitled to its performance; the knowledge of other sacrifices is of no use in that.

The following argument might be urged hereтАФтАЬWe have the injunction тАШthe entire Veda should be studied,тАЩ which pertains to the whole Veda, and implies the thorough understanding of the whole; and when it is necessary to understand the meaning of the entire Veda, how can there be any such partial knowledge as could justify such an assertion as that тАШhe who knows the meaning of the texts bearing on the Agnihotra shall be entitled to the performance of that act, even though he be ignorant of the meaning of other texts?тАЩтАЭ

Our answer to the above is as follows:тАФIt is the study of one Vedic Recension that is necessary; and what we mean is that he who has studied one Recension and has fully understood its meaning, becomes entitled to the performance of Vedic acts, even without studying the other Recensions.

тАЬThe purpose of the Scripture is the same in all cases; even though there may be some difference in the order of a few words and syllables, yet the main feature of the Scripture remains the same. Then again, as for the understanding of the meaning, this is obtained by the due comprehension of the meanings of words and reasonings; now, neither the meanings of words, nor the reasonings, differ in the different Recensions. So that the means by which one learns the meaning of one Recension serves the same purpose in regard to the other Recensions also; and one does not stand in need of any other learning; so that if One Recension has been learnt, all become learnt.тАЭ

True. Such Agnihotra, etc., as are enjoined in one Recension may not differ from the same acts as enjoined in other Recensions; but there are certain actions which are not enjoined at all in certain Recensions. E.g., the ┼Ъyena and other malevolent rites in connection with the Dar┼Ыa-p┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa are not found in the A┼Ыval─Бyana Recension of the с╣Ъgveda; nor the Somay─Бga, the V─Бjapeva, the Bс╣Ыhaspatisava and so forth. So that when a man has learnt one Recension, he becomes entitled to that Agnihotra and that Jyotiс╣гс╣нoma, etc., which are enjoined iu that Recension_(;) and if one who has not studied another Recension, and has neither read nor heard of it, how can he know anything about the acts enjoined in that other Recension? Nor ore the Soma-sacrifices compulsory; so that, through fear of incurring the sin of omitting a compulsory act, one might be forced to seek for the knowledge of them from other Recensions. As for the тАШKindling of Fire,тАЩ even though this also is not found enjoined in the said ─А┼Ыval─Бyana recension of the с╣Ъgveda, yet it does contain the injunction of preparing the тАШ─Аhavan─лyaтАЩ fire; as is clear from such passages as тАШbring up the ─Аhavan─лyaтАЩ; so that, not understanding the meaning of this passage with the help of ordinary people, the student naturally seeks, from other Recensions, for the knowledge of what this тАШ─Аhavan─лyaтАЩ is; and thus he comes to look over the entire section of the other Recension dealing with the тАШKindling of Fire.тАЩ Similarly having heard the passageтАФтАШHaving offered either the Am─Бv─Бsy─Б or the Paurс╣Зam─Бsa libations, etc.,тАЩ one seeks from other Recensions for the knowledge of the exact form of the two acts (of Am─Бv─Бsy─Б and Paurс╣Зam─Бsa offerings). Similarly in the case of other compulsory and optional acts that have to be performed, when it is found that some of their details arc not laid down in a certain Recension,тАФ-such details, for instance, as pertain to the Adhvaryu (and are mentioned in the Yajurveda) or to the Udg─Бtс╣Ы (and are mentioned in the S─Бma-Veda),тАФthe requisite knowledge is sought for from those other texts. It is not possible for one to know the act that is laid down in Recensions other than the one studied by him. To the student who learns several Recensions, and studies their meanings, all this becomes quite clear. But even in the absence of such knowledge as this last, the performance of acts is quite possible. Or, such performance could be possible even on a slight understanding (of the Vedic texts).

The sense of all this is that in the case of one whose learning is flawless, and who is fit to explain all sciences, such learning constitutes a title to respect.

тАШWeightier.тАЩтАФThe comparative ending indicates that the comparison is between two and two out of the five mentioned. Thus one who is fully versed in all the fourteeu sciences, is respected through his тАШlearning,тАЩ even though he he not entitled to it on account of being lame, blind or poor.

The text points out the relative superiority of these, with a view to cases where there may i.e a conflict among them.тАФ

тАШAmong these that which follow is weightier than that which precedes it.тАЩ For instance, when one man has vast wealth, and the other has many relations, then the latter deserves higher respect than the former; for that which follows is тАШweightierтАЩ than that which precedes it. Similarly Age is weightier than Relation. And from this it follows that Age is weightier still than Wealth. From all this it is clear that тАШLearning is superior to all, for all Dharma is based upon it,тАЩ as has been declared by Gautama (6-21тАФ22).

Objection.тАФтАЬSince the preceding factor is not weighty, how can we have the comparative form тАШweightierтАЩ? It is only when there are two weighty things that one can be called weightier; and since in the present case is, ex hypothesi, in relation to something preceding there can be no weightiness in тАШwealth,тАЩ which is not preceded by any thing else.тАЭ

What is meant is that the whole lot of five being тАШweightyтАЩ in common, the comparative ending is rightly used as showing that one is weightier than the other.

тАШM─БnaтАЩ means respect; тАШsth─БnaтАЩ means ground, cause.

If we adopt the reading тАШM─Бnyasth─Бn─Бni,тАЩ the term тАШm─БnyaтАЩ is to be explained as having the force of the abstract noun; тАШm─БnyaтАЩ standing for тАШm─Бnyatva.тАЩтАФ(136)

It has just been declared that among persons each of whom possesses only one of the qualifications mentioned, one possessing the latter is to be regarded as superior to one possessing the former. Now the question arisesтАФbetween two persons, one of whom possesses two former qualifications and the other possesses only one latter qualification, who is to be treated as superior? The following verse answers this question.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 474), where we find the following notes:тАФтАШVittamтАЩ stands for wealth acquired by lawful means;тАФтАШbandhuс╕етАЩ for uncles and others;тАФтАШvayaс╕етАЩ for older age;тАФтАШkarmaтАЩ for acts prescribed in the ┼Ъruti and Smс╣Ыti;тАФтАШvidy─БтАЩ for true knowledge;тАФthese are тАШm─Бnyasth─Бn─Бni,тАЩ i.e. grounds of respectability. (See note below on 137).

Apar─Бrka (p. 159) quotes this verse in support of the view that a man, though belonging to an inferior caste, deserves to be respected by another of the superior caste, if the former happens to be possessed of superior learning and other qualifications.тАФIt is quoted in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 44b);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 106), which explains тАШm─Бnyasth─Бn─БniтАЩ as тАШgrounds of respect, and adds that тАШlearningтАЩ is the highest of these all.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Viс╣гс╣Зu Smс╣Ыti (32.16)тАФ(words of Manu reproduced).

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra (6.20).тАФтАШWealth, Relationship, Caste, Learning and Age are objects of respect: the succeeding being superior to the preceding; Vedic Learning is superior to all, Dharma being based upon that.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti (1.3.21).тАФтАШLearning, Wealth, Age, Relationship and Deeds are objects of respect; when all these are present, the preceding has preference over the succeeding,тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.116).тАФтАШBy reason of Learning, Action, Age, Relationship, etc., and Wealth, in order, does a man become respected.тАЩ

B├╝hler

136 Wealth, kindred, age, (the due performance of) rites, and, fifthly, sacred learning are titles to respect; but each later-named (cause) is more weighty (than the preceding ones).

Among the three (higher) castes, he, in whom there are present most op these five, and of high degree, deserves (greater) respect; as also the ┼Ъ┼лdra who has reached the tenth stage (of life).тАФ(137)

  • рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрдгреЗрд╖реБ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╡реИрд╢реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдПрддреЗ рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рднреВрдпрд╛рдВрд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╢реН рдЪ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рд╣реАрдирдЧреБрдгреЗрди рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗрди рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпреБрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрдг рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рд░реН рдЕрдкрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╢реВрджреНрд░реЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рджрд╢рдореАрдореН рдЗрддрдГ ред рджрд╢рдореА рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдереЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдзрдХреЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН рдПрддрддреН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рддреНрддрдмрдиреНрдзреВ рд╢реВрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рди39 рдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╣реЗрддреВ рддреНрд░реИрд╡рд░реНрдгрд┐рдХрд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рддрд┐, рджрд╢рдореАрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрд╛рддреН ред рдХрд░реНрдорд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рдиреИрд╡ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддреЛ рд╜рдирдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН ред

  • рднреВрдпрд╛рдВрд╕реАрддреНрдпреН рдЖрдзрд┐рдХреНрдпрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдВ рди рдмрд╣реБрддреНрд╡рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпреИрд╡ ред рддреЗрди рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрддрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рди рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрдпрдВ рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпреЗрд╡ рдмрд╣реБрд╢рдмреНрдж рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рднреВрдпрдГрд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдпрдВ рди рдмрд╣реБрд╢рдмреНрдж рдЖрдзрд┐рдХреНрдпреЗ рдЪ рддрддреНрд░ рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред “рднреВрдпрд╛рдВрд╢реН рдЪрд╛рддреНрд░ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ,” “рднреВрдпрд╕рд╛рднреНрдпреНрджрдпреЗрди рдпреЛрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЗ” рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердмрд╣реБрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рди рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдореН ред “рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН” (рдкрд╛рдгреН рез.реи.релрео) рд╣реНрдпреН рдПрддрджреН рдмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдирдореН ред рд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐ рдПрдХрд╕реНрдп рдЧреБрдгрд╡рддреЛ рдорд╛рдирд╣реЗрддреБрддреНрд╡рдВ рди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рддрддрд╢реН рдЪ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛ рд╜рд╡рдЧрддрд┐рд░реН рдмрд╛рдзреНрдпрддреЗ40 ред рд╢реВрджреНрд░реЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рджрд╢рдореАрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЪ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рд╡рдпрд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗ рдорд╛рдирд╣реЗрддреБрддреНрд╡рдВ рдмреНрд░реБрд╡рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВ рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╢реН рдЪреИрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡ рее реи.резрейрен рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШOf these fiveтАЩ grounds of respect;тАФhe in whom there are тАШa larger numberтАЩтАФnot allтАФтАШdeserves respect.тАЩ And here the mere sequence (or posteriority) of the qualifications should not be much heeded. For instance, when one man possesses wealth and relations, and the other possesses only old age,тАФthe former gets preference over the latter.

But even when there are several qualities present, if they are not of high degree,тАФwhile the single quality possessed by the other person is of very high degree,тАФthen both are equal; and the larger number do not get over the latter (superior) qualification.

When the former verse uses the term тАШweightier,тАЩ it only means superiority in comparison to one (not several) of the preceding ones.

When however in one person there are a larger number of preceding qualities and also of high degree,тАФof great excellence,тАФwhile in the other person there are present the same number of succeeding qualities,тАФso that the number of preceding and succeeding qualifications (possessed by the two men) are equal,тАФthen, there is no getting over the one by the other, simply on the ground of precedence (in enumeration); in this case both are to he regarded as equal.

тАЬSince what the text declares is that he is deserving of respect in whom the qualities are of high degree,тАФit would he right to conclude that in the case just mentioned where the two persons possess an equal number of qualities (hut the preceding ones are of higher degree), the presence of the preceding set should get over the other.тАЭ

Not so; the epithet тАШof high degreeтАЩ is meant to apply to the case where the two sets of qualities are equal; e.g., where the one as well as the other is possessed of learning, superiority belongs to one whose learning is of the superior order. Similarly with the other qualities.

тАШAmong the three Castes,тАЩтАФi.e., among Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, Kс╣гatriyas and Vai┼Ыyas. If the said qualities, many in number and of high degree, belong to the Kс╣гatriya, then such a Kс╣гatriya deserves to be respected by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa possessed of inferior qualities, even though he belongs to the higher caste. The Vai┼Ыya, similarly, is to be respected by the Kс╣гatriya.

Similarly by all the twice-born castes the ┼Ъ┼лdra should be respected, тАШwhen he has reached the tenth stage.тАЩ The тАШtenthтАЩ stands for the last stage of life, and indicates extreme old age. Thus then, in case of the ┼Ъ┼лdra, тАШwealthтАЩ and тАШrelationsтАЩ do not constitute grounds of respect, in relation to tho three higher castes. This is clear from the fact, that the Text specifies the тАШtenth stage.тАЩ тАШActionтАЩ and тАШLearningтАЩ are not possible in the ┼Ъ┼лdra; for the simple reason that he is not entitled to these.

тАШMostтАЩ;тАФall that is meant by this is excess, not plurality of number (which would mean at least three); hence what is asserted applies to tho presence of qualities also. There is nothing to justify the notion that the term тАШbahuтАЩ (from which тАШbh┼лy─Бmsi is derivedтАЩ) denotes number. Further, the term actually used is тАШbh┼лyaс╕е,тАЩ not тАШb─БhuтАЩ; and the former is often found to be used in the sense of excess, much: e.g., тАШbh┼лy─Бс╣Е┼Ыch─Бtra parih─Бro,тАЩ тАШthere is much that can be said in answer to this,тАЩ тАШbh┼лy─Бbhyudayena yokс╣гye,’ тАШI shall become endowed with much prosperity.тАЩ Nor is any significance meant to be attached to the plural number in тАШbh┼лy─БmsiтАЩ; the plural number in this case denoting only kind, according to P─Бс╣Зini 3.2.58, which lays down that тАШwhen a kind or genus is spoken of, the plural number is optionally used.тАЩ If significance were really meant to be attached to the plural number, then a person possessed of only one quality (of however high degree) would never be entitled to respect; and this would run counter to what we h ave learnt from the foregoing verse. Furthor, by speaking of тАФтАШthe ┼Ъ┼лdra who has reached the tenth stageтАЩтАФwhere mere age (only one quality) is mentioned as a ground of respect,тАФthe Text has made it clear that no significance is meant to be attached to the plural number (in тАШbh┼лy─БmsiтАЩ). Usage also points to the same conclusion.тАФ(1.37)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted along with verse 136 in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 474), which adds the following explanation:тАФAmong the three castes, Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, Kс╣гatriya and Vai┼Ыya, the person who possesses a greater amount of the preceding qualification (among the five mentioned in 136) is to be honoured more than one possessed of the succeeding one only. Thus a person possessed of greater wealth and superior relations is higher than one only older in age; one possessed of a higher degree of wealth, relations and age is higher than one superior in action only;тАФone possessed in a higher degree of wealth, relation, age and action is superior to one possessing learning only;тАФтАШguс╣ЗavantiтАЩ means superior; which means that between two persons possessing wealth, he is higher whose wealth is superior; and the тАШsuperiorityтАЩof wealth would consist in its having been acquired by lawful means and such other circumstaс╣Зces. In the case of тАШrelations,тАЩ this superiority would consist in being more intimate and so forth;тАФin the case of тАШageтАЩ it would consist in being very much older;тАФin that of тАШaction,тАЩ in its being equipped with all auxiliary details;тАФin that of тАШlearning,тАЩ in its being acquired in the prescribed manner.тАФтАШTenth stageтАЩ stands for the age over ninety years; the hundred years of manтАЩs life being divided into ten equal spans, the tenth one coming after the ninetieth year;тАФ-when he has reached this age, the ┼Ъ┼лdra also becomes entitled to honour at the hands of the twice-born.

The last foot of the verse regarding the тАШtenth stageтАЩ is quoted on p. 453 also, as declaring the respectability of the ┼Ъ┼лdra.

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 159), where тАШda┼Ыam─лтАЩ is explained as тАШthe last ten years of the hundred yearsтАЩ;тАФтАШbh┼лy─Бс╣ГsiтАЩ as to number and тАШguс╣ЗavantiтАЩ as to degree;тАФhence without considering the caste, one possessed of superior learning is to he respected by another possessed of less; or one who knows more subjects is to be respected by another knowing a lesser number; similarly in regard to тАШkarmaтАЩ and other qualifications also;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 48), which explains тАШda┼Ыam─лm gataс╕етАЩ as тАШover ninety years of age,тАЩ and тАШpa├▒ch─Бn─БmтАЩ as тАШamong learning and the restтАЩ;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 106), which explains тАШda┼Ыam─лтАЩ as тАШthe last part of hundred years, i. e. beyond ninety years,тАЩ and adds that тАШold ageтАЩ is meant to be indicative of the presence of wealth and the rest also.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra (10.6).тАФтАШThe ┼Ъ┼лdra also if he has children and is over 80 years in age.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (1.116).тАФтАШWhen the said qualities (of Learning, etc.) are present in a very large degree, the ┼Ъ┼лdra also deserves respect, when he has reached old age.тАЩ

B├╝hler

137 Whatever man of the three (highest) castes possesses most of those five, both in number and degree, that man is worthy of honour among them; and (so is) also a Sudra who has entered the tenth (decade of his life).

  • рдирдиреБ рдЪреЛрдкрдХреНрд░рдореЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрд╛рджреН рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдЧрддрдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реН рддрддреНрдкрд░ рдПрд╡ рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ ред рд░рд╛рдЬрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд╣рд┐ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рддрд┐рд╡рдЪрдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрдГ ред рд╕ рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдЕрдиреБрдкрдЬрд╛рддрд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЙрдкрдХреНрд░рдордЧрддреЛ рдореБрдЦреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдпрдГ ред рдмрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпреЗ рддреБ рддрддреНрд╕рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рддрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддреЗрди рдзрд░реНрдореЗрдг рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрди рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрд╕рдВрднрд╡реЗрди рдЬрд╛рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред

  • рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрддрд╛рддреНрд░ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд╛ ред рд╕реНрдирд╛рддрдХреЛ рдиреГрдкрдорд╛рдирднрд╛рдЧреАрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрдирд╛рддрдХрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН рдПрд╡, “рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдВ рджрд╢рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдореН” (рдореНрдзреН реи.резрейрел) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╣рд┐ рднреВрдорд┐рдкрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рддрд┐рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЛрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрде рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЙрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рд░рд╛рдЬрдЬрд╛рддреЗрдГ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдВ рдзрд░реНрдореЛ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред

  • рд╡рд░реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрдГ ред рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрдиреНрдерд╛ рджреЗрдпрдГ ред рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рдЪ рджрджрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрд╢реН рдЪ рдкрдереЛ рд╜рдкрд╕рд░рдгрдореН ред рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереА рди рдХреГрддрд╛ рее реи.резрейрео рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Another method of showing respect is also described by the way.

тАШChakrinтАЩ is the person in a chariot, one who is occupying a cart or some such conveyance. For him тАШway should be made.тАЩ тАШWayтАЩ is that path, that part of the Earth, by which one goes to a village and such other places; while one is on such a тАШway,тАЩ if a man in a chariot should happen to come either in front of him or behind him, then the man on foot should move off from the spot where he might be obstructing the passing of the cart.

тАШOne who is in the tenth stage of lifeтАЩтАФone who is far advanced in age.

тАШOne suffering from a diseaseтАЩтАФone who is suffering very badly from some malady.

тАШOne who is carrying a burdenтАЩтАФone who is carrying grains and other heavy things; such a man also finds it difficult to move, and hence must bo favoured.

тАШA woman,тАЩтАФi.e., simply by reason of her being a woman, irrespective of her caste or qualifications, or of the position of her husband.

тАШKingтАЩтАФstands here for the master of a kingdom, not for the mere Kс╣гatriya. For in the conclusion (which comes in the next verse) we have the term тАШP─БrthivaтАЩ which means the тАШlord of the Earth,тАЩ тАШpс╣Ыthivy─Бс╕е ─л┼Ыvaraс╕е.тАЩ

Objection.тАФтАЬIn as much as in the opening verse (the present) we have the term тАШr─Бjan,тАЩ it would be more reasonable to interpret the term тАШparthivaтАЩ (in the next verse) in accordance with, and as standing for, the тАШR─Бj─БтАЩ (than that тАШR─Бj─БтАЩ should be taken as standing for the тАШp─БrthivaтАЩ), and the word тАШR─БjanтАЩ is well-known as denoting the Kс╣гatriya caste; and as this forms the principal denotation of the term, it should be accepted in the opening of the passage, specially as there does not appear to be any incongruity in it. In the next verse, where the relative merits are mentioned, it is quite possible to take the term тАШparthivaтАЩ as referring to the Kс╣гatriya; in view of the fact that the тАШprotecting of the Earth,тАЩ which is connoted by the term тАШp─Бrtiva.тАЩ is a duty prescribed specifically for the Kс╣гatriya. So that it cannot be right, to take the term as referring to other castes, merely on the strength of their being тАШin possession of landтАЩ (тАШpс╣Ыth─лvy─Бс╕е ─л┼Ыvaraс╕етАЩ).тАЭ

To the above we make the following reply:тАФWhat is asserted here (in the next verse) is capability being respected;тАФwhen, e.g., the person who has just passed out of hi s studentship is described as deserving to be honoured by a king. Under verse 35, it has been pointed out that the term тАШbh┼лmipaтАЩ stands for the Kс╣гatriya caste; and since the Kingly caste is merely indicative, what is mentioned here is understood to pertain to such a Kс╣гatriya as happens to be the тАШlord of men.тАЩ

The тАШbridegroomтАЩтАФwho is going to marry. For these persons тАШway should be made;тАЩтАФwhat is meant by тАШdeyaс╕е,тАЩ тАШshould be made,тАЩ is simply that one should give up the road; and as тАШgiving upтАЩ only means moving off (and not actual giving), the Dative ending has not been used.тАФ(138)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 76);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 48), which explains тАШvaraс╕етАЩ as тАШone who is going to marryтАЩ;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 107), which has the following notesтАФтАШchakrin,тАЩ one who is driving in a cart,тАФтАШsn─Бtaka,тАЩ the student who has completed his course of studentship,тАФтАШvaraс╕е,тАЩ one who is going to marry;тАФwhen one meets any of these, he should make way for him, i.e., move away from his path,тАФamong those mentioned here, the Accomplished Student and the King deserve to be respected by the тАШothersтАЩ, as stated in the next verse.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 138-139)
**

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti (13.25, 26).тАФтАШAmong the followingтАФan aged person, a child, a sick person, a man carrying a load, a woman, a man driving in a chariot,тАФthe succeeding should make way for the preceding; when the King and the Accomplished Student meet, the king should make way for the student; all should make way for a bride who is being married.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 6. 25, 26.тАФтАШOne on a chariot, a man in the tenth stage of life, one who deserves kindness (i.e., the sick), a bride, an Accomplished Student, and the King,тАФfor these way should he made; the King should make way for the Vedic scholar.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 2. 3. 50 (also Devala quoted in V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 476).тАФтАШWay should he made for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the cow, the king, the blind person, the aged, the man suffering under a load, a pregnant woman and a weak person.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 2. 2. 57.тАФтАШWay should be made for the King until he meets the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; but when he meets the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, way should be made for the latter. All men should make way for a conveyance, for one carrying a load, one struck with disease, and a woman; to one of superior caste; and also to the Renunciate, and the intoxicated and the lunatic,тАФthese latter for the sake of oneтАЩs own safety.тАЩ

M─Бrkaс╣Зс╕Нeya Pur─Бс╣Зa (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, 6.475).тАФтАШWay should be made for the dumb, the blind, the deaf, the intoxicated, the lunatic, the loose woman, oneтАЩs enemy, a child and the outcast.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha-Likhita (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 476).тАФтАШWay should be made for the child, the aged, the intoxicated, the lunatic, one struck with a foul disease, one carrying a load, a woman who is pregnant, the Accomplished Student, the Renunciate, and also persons excelling in learning, arts and other qualities.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 476).тАФтАШWay should be made for the aged, the man with a load, the King, the Accomplished Student, a woman, the sick, the bridegroom, the man on a chariot; among these the King deserves special honour; but the Accomplished Student deserves honour even from the King.тАЩ

B├╝hler

138 Way must be made for a man in a carriage, for one who is above ninety years old, for one diseased, for the carrier of a burden, for a woman, for a Snataka, for the king, and for a bridegroom.

Among these, when they come together, the man who has just passed his studentship and the King deserve to be honoured; and between the person just passed his studentship and the King, the person just passed his studentship receives the respects op the King.тАФ(139)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШAmong these, when they come together,тАЩтАФwhen they happen to meet,тАФтАШthe person just passed his studentship and the King deserve to he honouredтАЩтАФby the тАШmaking of way,тАЩ which is the particular form of тАШhonouringтАЩ mentioned in the present context.

тАШReceives the respects of the KingтАЩтАФi.e., obtains honour from the King.

The genitive case-ending has the sense of selection (according to P─Бс╣Зini 2.3.41)

Among the restтАФthe person riding a chariot and othersтАФthere is option, dependent upon their respective capacity.тАФ(139)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse also is simply quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 477);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 107) to the effect that among the persons mentioned in the preceding verse the accomplished student and the king deserve to be respected by the othersтАЩ, and between these two the former is to be respected by the latter.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(verses 138-139)

B├╝hler

139 Among all those, if they meet (at one time), a Snataka and the king must be (most) honoured; and if the king and a Snataka (meet), the latter receives respect from the king.
